https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/SitePages/Add-a-Conference-Room-to-a-Teams-Meeting.aspx https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/SitePages/How-to-use-a-Microsoft-Teams-Room-Device.aspx

 

This guide is for using the Cumberland Room for meetings.

How to add the Conference Room to a meeting already scheduled or in progress. Click Here


The Cumberland Room has a Teams Room System that is can conduct Teams Meetings, Zoom Meetings, and Cisco Webex Meetings. 

For information on using a Team Room System for Online Meetings. Click Here

​​​​​​​

The room also can do In Room Only Meetings allowing content to be placed on either TV.

As you enter Cumberland-14 through the door closest to elevators, the Conference Room System Touch panel is immediately on the right.  If the Touch Panel screen is blank, then touch it to wake up the Conference Room System.

Cumberland Room has two HDMI connections, one in each table.  Two TV’s, one in front of the tables and one to the side.  One camera located above the TV on the short wall.  The Conference Room is controlled by the Conference Room Touch Panel on the short wall as you enter from the door closest to the elevators. If the Touch Panel screen is blank, then touch it to wake up the Conference Room System.

​​​​​​​Conference Room Microphones:

The Conference Room Microphones are muted by default for Online Meetings.  When your Teams Meetings starts, you will need to unmute the Room Microphones by touching the outer ring of one of the Room Microphones.

Below shows the Microphones Muted (RED RING) - Touch outer ring to Un-Mute Room Microphones.

Below shows the Microphones Un-Muted (GREEN RING) - Touch outer ring to Mute Room Microphones.

Non-Teams Meeting:

(In Room Only Meetings), are controlled from the Room System Touch Panel on the wall.  Press Room Controls shown below in yellow to change HDMI or TV options.


​​​​​​​From the ribbon at the bottom, you can control Teams Meetings, Power, Presentation (In Room Only Meetings), Camera, and Displays.

You do not need to power the system On or Off as it will go to sleep automatically.  Touching the Touch Panel wakes the system up.

In Room Only Presentations:

In each table there are HDMI cables for in room only presentations.  HDMI cables are NOT needed for Teams Meetings.  Showing content on the Conference Room TV’s while in a Teams Meeting is handled by the Teams Client.  The Conference Room is a participant in a Teams Meeting just like remote participants.  Connect either HDMI cable to the presenter's laptop.

Once HDMI cable is connected. On the Conference Room Touch Panel press Room Controls then press Presentation located in the middle of the bottom ribbon.

If the presenter's laptop is plugged into Laptop 2 in the table.  Press Laptop 2 button at top, then press Send to Both to send to both TV’s.  You can also choose to Laptop 2 then Press Monitor 2 to only send Laptop 2 screen to Monitor 2 which is the TV on the Short Wall. 

Or press Monitor 1 to send Laptop 2 to the TV on the long wall.  If you have laptop plugged into Laptop 1 you can select Laptop 1 and Send to Both or Choose which Monitor to send the signal to.  These settings are not needed for Teams Meetings.

Wireless 1 and Wireless 2 DO NOT Work and will be removed from the selection at a future date.

​​​​​​​For In Room Only Presentations that include Audio:

Connect laptop to either or HDMI connection in Tables.  On the laptop change audio playback device.  In the bottom right-hand corner of laptop screen select the audio icon.

​​​​​​​Change Playback Device to Crestron 420 (Intel(R) Display Audio).

To change the Camera view, press the Camera button. Camera is only used in Online Meetings.

​​​​​​​If a TV is off for some reason, you can turn it back on.  There is no reason to turn TV’s off after meetings as the system sleeps automatically. TV's are controlled by the Display button on far right.

​​​​​​​The power button should not be needed, the Room will automatically sleep and wake up again when the Room System Touch Panel is Touched.

This guide is for using Shelby-15 A Room for meetings.


For how to use both Shelby-15 A and Shelby-15 B together for a large meeting. Click Here

How to add the Conference Room to a meeting already scheduled or in progress. Click Here


The Shelby-15 A Room has a Teams Room System that is can conduct Teams Meetings, Zoom Meetings, and Cisco Webex Meetings.

For information on using a Team Room System for Online Meetings. Click Here


Shelby-15 A Room Layout:

Shelby-15 A HDMI Connections:

Shelby-15 A has two HDMI connections. One on the wall beneath the touch panel, and one under the table.  Shown in diagram above.  There is also one under the table in a floor receptacle.  Flip up the receptable to access the HDMI Floor outlet along with additional power and network.

Additional Power:

​​​​​​​Shelby-15 A Conference Room contains 2 “Power Poles” for additional power as needed.  When your meeting is finished, please return them.

Using Shelby-15 A for Meetings:

For Teams / Zoom / and Cisco Webex only meetings. Click Here

​​​​​​​Non-Team Meetings:

(In Room Only Meetings), are controlled from the Room System Touch Panel on the wall.  Press Room Control shown below in yellow to change HDMI or TV options.



Select Display Source:

Wall Laptop: is the HDMI connection under the Room System Touch Panel. 

Floor Laptop: is the HDMI connection under table. 

Wireless: is for Wireless Display connection. 

Connect the HDMI cable to laptop and select the source.  You can also press Wireless Source on touch panel to connect via wireless display.

This is all controlled from the Presentation button shown in Yellow.

Audio Source:

If you are showing a Video or need sound from the HDMI connection.  Press the Laptop Audio button. 

For In Room Only Presentations that include Audio, Non-Online Meetings:

Connect laptop to either of the HDMI connections.  On the laptop change audio playback device.  In the bottom right-hand corner of laptop screen select the audio icon.

Change Playback Device to Crestron 420 (Intel(R) Display Audio).

Presentation button is NOT needed for Online Meetings.

Camera Controls: Do NOT Manually Move Camera.

Press Room Controls, then Select Camera in the bottom ribbon.  Here you will be able to move the camera.  After your meeting is finished press Preset 1 to return camera to default position.

​​​​​​​Once your In Room Only Meeting is finished. Press Conferencing to return to Teams Room System Application.

Please call the helpdesk 1-615-770-8601 if you have any questions.

This guide is for using the Shelby Rooms A and B in combined mode (Room Partition Removed)

Always invite both Shelby-15 A and Shelby-15 B to your meeting.  This will reserve both room and prevent conference room reservation issues.


How to add the Conference Room to a meeting already scheduled or in progress. Click Here.  When in Combined mode add CR Shelby-15 A to the Teams Meeting.

The Shelby Rooms has a Teams Room System that is can conduct Teams Meetings, Zoom Meetings, and Cisco Webex Meetings. 

For information on using a Team Room System for Online Meetings. Click Here


Opening The Wall Partition:  Recommended two-person job.

Enter Shelby-15 B and find the "partition tool".

Insert the partition tool into the wall socket while on Shelby-15 B, shown in yellow below

Turn counterclockwise to shrink the partition so it can be moved. Turn reverse of Extend.

Slide one wall partition section toward the opening and pull the right side along the track. Then push into opening in room to store the wall partitions.

To return room to working order, reverse all instructions.


While in Combined Mode:

Shelby-15 A Teams Room System Touch Panel controls whole room, shown below in yellow. Shelby-15 B touch panel is NOT used.

Shelby-15 B touch panel will be unavailable to use.

Using Shelby-15 A/B in Combined Mode for Online Meetings:

For Teams / Zoom / and Cisco Webex only meetings. Click Here Always add participant or join room audio as Shelby-15 A.  Shelby-15 B is not used while in Combined Mode.


Non-Teams Meeting:

(In Room Only Meetings), are controlled from the Shelby-15 A Room System Touch Panel on the wall.  Press Room Controls shown below in yellow to change HDMI or TV options.



Select Display Source:

While in Combined Mode there are 4 HDMI connections possible, while only two can be used at a time. 

HDMI cables are NOT needed for Teams Meetings.  Showing content on the Conference Room TV’s while in a Teams Meeting is handled by the Teams Client.  The Conference Room is a participant in a Teams Meeting just like remote participants.  Connect either HDMI cable to the presenter's laptop.

Once HMDI cable is connected.  On the Shelby-15 A Touch Panel press Room Controls, then press Presentation if needed (on bottom ribbon).

Shelby-15 A Wall HDMI Connected:

Press Rm A Wall Laptop and press Send To All to send presentation to both Room Monitors.  Or select an individual monitor by pressing RM A Monitor or RM B Monitor to only send signal to particular Monitor.

Shelby-15 A Floor HDMI Connected:

Press Rm A Floor Laptop and press Send To All to send presentation to both Room Monitors.  Or select an individual monitor by pressing RM A Monitor or RM B Monitor to only send signal to particular Monitor.

Shelby-15 B Wall HDMI Connected:

Press Rm B Wall Laptop and press Send To All to send presentation to both Room Monitors.  Or select an individual monitor by pressing RM A Monitor or RM B Monitor to only send signal to particular Monitor.

Shelby-15 B Floor HDMI Connected:

Press Rm B Floor Laptop and press Send To All to send presentation to both Room Monitors.  Or select an individual monitor by pressing RM A Monitor or RM B Monitor to only send signal to particular Monitor.


For In Room Only Presentations that include Audio, Non-Online Meetings:

Connect laptop to either or HDMI connection in Tables.  On the laptop change audio playback device.  In the bottom right-hand corner of laptop screen select the audio icon.

Change Playback Device to Crestron 420 (Intel(R) Display Audio).

Select Audio Source:

Camera Controls: Do NOT Physically move camera.

Only Shelby-15 A camera is active while in Combined Mode.

This guide is for using Shelby-15 B Room for meetings.


For how to use both Shelby-15 A and Shelby-15 B together for a large meeting. Click Here

How to add the Conference Room to a meeting already scheduled or in progress. Click Here


The Shelby-15 B Room has a Teams Room System that is can conduct Teams Meetings, Zoom Meetings, and Cisco Webex Meetings.

For information on using a Team Room System for Online Meetings. Click Here
 


Shelby-15 B Room Layout:
 

Shelby-15 B HDMI Connections:

Shelby-15 B has two HDMI connections. One on the wall beneath the touch panel, and one under the table.  Shown in diagram above.  There is also one under the table in a floor receptacle.  Flip up the receptable to access the HDMI Floor outlet along with additional power and network.

Additional Power:

​​​​​​​Shelby-15 B Conference Room contains 2 “Power Poles” for additional power as needed.  When your meeting is finished, please return them.

Using Shelby-15 B for Meetings:

For Teams / Zoom / and Cisco Webex only meetings. Click Here

​​​​​​​Non-Team Meetings:

(In Room Only Meetings), are controlled from the Room System Touch Panel on the wall.  Press Room Control shown below in yellow to change HDMI or TV options.



Select Display Source:

Wall Laptop: is the HDMI connection under the Room System Touch Panel. 

Floor Laptop: is the HDMI connection under table. 

Wireless: is for Wireless Display connection. 

Connect the HDMI cable to laptop and select the source.  You can also press Wireless Source on touch panel to connect via wireless display.

This is all controlled from the Presentation button shown in Yellow.

Audio Source:

If you are showing a Video or need sound from the HDMI connection.  Press the Laptop Audio button. 

For In Room Only Presentations that include Audio, Non-Online Meetings:

Connect laptop to either of the HDMI connections.  On the laptop change audio playback device.  In the bottom right-hand corner of laptop screen select the audio icon.

Change Playback Device to Crestron 420 (Intel(R) Display Audio).
 

Presentation button is NOT needed for Online Meetings.

Camera Controls: Do NOT Manually Move Camera.

Press Room Controls, then Select Camera in the bottom ribbon.  Here you will be able to move the camera.  After your meeting is finished press Preset 1 to return camera to default position.

Once your In Room Only Meeting is finished. Press Conferencing to return to Teams Room System Application.
 

Please call the helpdesk 1-615-770-8601 if you have any questions.

http://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Overviews/Welcome_to_TeamWorks.htm http://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Info_Exchange_Twelfth_Edition/index.htm http://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Cloud/desktop/Overviews/Welcome_to_Newforma_Project_Cloud.htm

With the Newforma Capture app for your iOS device, you're always ready to create new project items on the job site supplemented by photos. Using the Newforma Capture app, you can:

  • Quickly create and log action items, field notes, and punch lists and upload them to their corresponding projects in Newforma Project Center and Newforma Info Exchange, or Newforma ConstructEx.
  • Ensure your project team has access to project items immediately.

When you create a new project item and upload it, it is automatically added to the project you selected and its corresponding activity center (the Action Items, Field Notes, or Punch Lists activity center) in both Newforma Info Exchange and Newforma Project Center (or Newforma ConstructEx) and is immediately available in both. Project Center and Info Exchange users can then view and edit the items (based on their permissions).

After you upload items from the Capture app, the items are automatically removed from the app and are then only available in Project Center and Info Exchange, or Newforma ConstructEx.

Project access

If a project is not in the list of projects, notify your contact at the company that is hosting the project on their Info Exchange website. Ask them to alert their Newforma Project Center administrator. This may occur for the following reasons:

  • If a single project is missing for a specific company, you may not have Info Exchange access to the specific project.
  • If all projects are missing for a specific company, it is likely the customer has not installed a Newforma Project Center Twelfth Edition license that enables Newforma ID. If the company is not available as a connection, contact the Newforma administrator for the company hosting the projects on Newforma Info Exchange to install a Twelfth Edition license.

Free accounts can only use one project at a time. Upgrade or remove the project to add another project.

To Start Using Capture

1. Before launching Capture, you can configure how it starts. In Settings, select whether Capture always starts in camera mode (on), or by selecting a project and choosing how to log an item (off, which is the default) as shown here:

2. Launch the Capture app and login using your Newforma ID.

3. From the main screen, tap (which is next to Items to Upload in the upper left) to begin capturing a new project item. You have three options for capturing and logging an item:

  • Create a Project item with a new photo
  • Create a project item with a photo from your device's Camera Roll
  • Create a project item without a photo

To Create a Project Item from a New Photo

1. From the New Item panel, tap to launch the camera on your device.

2. Take the photo. The photo is attached to the item, as shown here:

3. Tap Select a Project to open the Change Type panel to select the project and the type of item to create, as shown here:

If you previously entered an item, the new item type defaults to the previously entered item's project and type. In this case you would tap the area listing the item type (such as Field Note) instead of Select a Project to change the project and type, as shown here:

4. Tap the project to which you want to add the new item. The Change Type panel now shows the name of the selected project and the available project item types for that project, as shown here:

Non-compliance is a type of punch list and if selected, would be added to the Punch Lists activity center.

5. Tap the type of item you want to create. For this example, we'll create an action item, as shown in this example:

6. Tap the fields to which you want to add information.

7. Tap Save to add the new item to the Items to Upload list in the main Capture panel, as shown here:

8. To upload the new item immediately to Project Center and Info Exchange, tap next to the item.

After you upload an item, it is removed from the Capture app and can no longer be accessed from it. You can wait until you are finished adding items and then click Upload All to upload them all at once.

To create a project item from an image in your device's Camera Roll

1. Start with the To Start Using Capture section above.

2. From the New Item panel, tap to open the Photos panel, as shown here, which displays your photos.

3. Tap an image to attach it to the new item.

4. Perform the steps in the previous section above starting with step 3.

To create a project item without a photo

1. Start with the To Start Using Capture section above.

2. Perform the steps in the To Create a section above starting with step 3 (skip the photo steps).

To view and edit your project items

1. To view an item, tap the one you want to view from the list under Items to Upload to open its Edit Item panel to view and edit its details, as shown here:

2. Tap any of the fields you wish to edit and make your changes.

3. Tap any of the buttons at the bottom of the panel, as shown here, to email the item or add additional photos to it.


  • Red square - use to email the item
  • Purple square - use to add additional photos from camera roll
  • Yellow square - use to add additional photos by taking a new picture

4. To remove a photo, long press its icon and tap Remove Media, as shown here:

To email a single project item

From the Items to Upload panel, tap the desired project item, then tap to open a new email message. Enter any details pertaining to the item and tap Send to send the message to another contact. The email message will contain the details of the item and any photos.

To remove a single project item

Slide the item to the left to enable the Delete option, then tap it, as shown in this example:

To upload all project items to Info Exchange and Project Center at once

From the bottom of the Items to Upload panel, tap Upload All. The items will be removed from the Capture app once they are uploaded.

Common Questions & Answers

Can I download and edit existing project items?

No, Capture is used only for creating and uploading new items. 

Does the Capture app automatically upload my items?

No, you have to manually upload your new project items. This allows the app to be more responsive so you can move quickly through the site without having to deal with it syncing all the time.

How can I change my default capture settings?

Go to settings to select whether Capture always starts in camera mode (on) or to start by selecting a project and choosing how to log an item (off, which is the default) as shown here:

Can I select multiple spaces?

Yes.

Newforma Email Filing Function

File Email Messages from Outlook to Project Center

Perform the following steps to file Microsoft Outlook email messages to a Project Center project.

To file project email

1.     In Microsoft Outlook, select the email messages you want to file to a Project Center project.

2.     Click File in Project from the legacy Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook Ribbon Bar to open the File in Project dialog box, as shown here:


3.     From the Project drop-down list, select the project you want to file the email message to. The Default Project Location is the default folder in which the .MSG file will be saved. If you want to save it to another location or project item, choose the Another Project Location option and select a recent location or item from the drop-down list, or click the 

  icon to select another project location or item.

If you file an Outlook item to the wrong project and want to move it to a different project, select the item in the Project Email activity center, then click Explorer Tasks > Move from the Email Tasks panel to move it.

4.     Mark the Select in Project Center After Filing checkbox if you want to open Project Center to the message's location after filing it.

5.     Click OK to save the email message file to the selected project (and project item if applicable). You can then add it to any Project Center item from Project Center, and it can be searched.

When filing email messages from your email client, Categories/Keywords are filed as keywords in Project Center. When messages are re-filed, the existing keywords are not overwritten. Note that you cannot manually enter a custom keyword.

When a user files an email message that is a duplicate of another email message already filed in the same project folder, the original is overwritten.

You can also file messages by moving them into special folders inside of Outlook. See File Email Items Automatically Using the Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook for more information.

If you use Outlook with an IMAP email server, be aware that categories will not be saved when filing email messages into Project Center.



File Email Items Automatically Using the Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook

Using the Synchronize button, the legacy Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook enables you to file large numbers of email items from Microsoft Outlook to multiple Project Center projects at once. You can drag and drop large numbers of email items into the Project Center project folders under the Newforma - Items to File folder in Outlook to have them filed automatically in the corresponding Project Center project.

When you click the Synchronize button in the legacy Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook Ribbon Bar, a top-level folder called Newforma - Items to File is created in your email client (if it's not already there), and subfolders for each project listed in your My Projects tab of the My Project Center activity center are added under the Newforma - Items to File folder, as shown in the following example. When projects are subsequently added, deleted, and updated in your My Projects tab, they are also updated accordingly under this folder when Synchronize is clicked.

For the project folders to appear under the Newforma - Items to File folder, the corresponding projects must be in your My Projects tab in Project Center. To add projects to your My Projects tab, click the All Projects tab, select the project, then click Add to My Projects from the Tasks panel.


Administrators can change the names of the project subfolders listed under the Newforma - Items to File folder in the Email Folder Label field of the Edit Project Settings dialog box Admin tab. Do not change the names of the project subfolders by right-clicking on them and choosing Rename!

Dragging and dropping email messages

After the project folders are created, you can drag and drop as many Outlook email messages as you want into the Project Center project folders under the Newforma - Items to File folder.

Tagged email messages filed to a project are filed to the designated action items, submittals, RFIs, and timeline items.

You can only drag and drop email messages into the project folders under Newforma - Items to File. You cannot drag and drop email items such as tasks and calendar items.

Depending on your system's configuration, you may see additional features when dragging and dropping emails to file:

●        Emails filed will include any previous conversations connected to that email message

●        Emails filed will show filed for others as well

For questions on your system's email configuration, please reach out to your Global Administrator. You can also refer to Configure Graph API Auto Email Filing.

Two-way communication

If you subsequently add, remove, or rename any projects in the My Projects tab of the My Project Center activity center, the project folders are updated accordingly under the Newforma - Items to File folder in Outlook each time you click the Synchronize button. Any email items subsequently moved into these project folders in Outlook are filed in each corresponding project's default project email folder, which is configured in the Project Email Settings section of the Create Project dialog box or the Edit Project Settings dialog box.

Automatic filing vs. clicking the Synchronize button

By default, Project Center is configured to file email messages in the Newforma - Items to File folder automatically at a set interval. However, you can file items manually by clicking the Synchronize button.

You cannot file items manually if the Project Center Server is in the process of automatically filing your items, in which case you are told who is doing the filing.

●        When you click the Synchronize button, the items are filed and sub-folders are created for each project listed in the Project Center My Projects tab.

    • If you add a new project to the My Projects tab, it is added to the list in Outlook.
    • If you remove a project from the My Projects tab, the items are filed, then the project is removed from the list in Outlook once the folder is empty. Project Center never removes a folder from Outlook until it is empty.
    • If you change the Email Folder Label in the Admin tab of Edit Project Settings dialog box, the items are filed, then the project is renamed to this label in the list in Outlook.
    • If an administrator adds sub-folders in the Project Folders tab of the Edit Project Settings dialog box, the folders are added to the Outlook list if you have write-access to them.

●        Email items are copied from the Project Center folders in Outlook to the default project email folder and subfolders (if defined).

Project Center creates and manages the folders. Do not create or delete folders under the Newforma – Items to File folder.

When filing email messages from your email client, Categories/Keywords are filed as keywords in Project Center. When messages are re-filed, any new keywords are merged with the existing keywords.

Multiple tags

Email messages support multiple tags, which means they can be filed to multiple project items, and by multiple companies using Project Center. For example, an email message that has been filed to an action item by company A can then be filed to a submittal and RFI by company A, and can also be filed by other companies that use Project Center.

Other Features

●        Mobile support – you can drag files into folders on a mobile device or on a disconnected laptop, then click Synchronize when you are connected.

●        Outlook Web Access support – you can drag files to folders viewable in Outlook Web Access and then file them.

Tips

●        If you want to keep items in your Outlook Inbox, you can press Ctrl while dragging to copy the files into the folders and leave the originals where they are.

●        If a project’s Email Folder Label is changed in the Admin tab of Edit Project Settings dialog box, the corresponding email folder is also renamed.

●        Changing an Email Folder Label (and therefore its corresponding email folder) can result in filing problems on some mobile devices. Switching off and restarting the mobile device should resolve the problem.

Permissions and confidentiality

●        If you do not have write permissions to write to a folder (for example, a confidential folder), the folder will not appear under the Newforma - Items to File folder.

●        If you have access to write to a folder, then the Project Center service account also has to have write permissions to be able to file the message.  

●        If permissions to a confidential folder have changed, the folder is either added or removed from the list.

●        Access to confidential folders can be restricted through operating system permissions.

●        Project email and search respect operating system permissions on file system folders to limit access to these confidential email messages.

●        Administrators can add confidential and other alternate email folders to Project Center using the Edit Project Email Folders dialog box.

Dimensions: 1800x823

With the ever expanding use of Newforma across the firm, we have arrived at the point where it is necessary to start archiving Newforma projects. We will address the criteria used to determine what projects get archived, along with information on how this will affect user access to project information.

First question inevitably is, "When will my project be archived?". The Newforma Project Center server gives us several metrics that we can use to determine when a project has been updated, modified or accessed.  Using the Last Accessed metric allows us to determine the last time the project was opened by a project team member or user. Currently, the standard of when a project will be archived is when a project hasn't been accessed for a year.

When the project is archived, it will be put into an "Archive" status in Newforma Project Center (Fig. 1),



and the files associated with the project will be relocated to the nfarc network file location (Fig. 2 & 3).



All the project information will be available to view and reference from Newforma Project Center, in the same way as "Active" projects. One crucial difference is that files will become read only, and project functions like Transmittals, Info Exchange, RFIs, etc., will no longer be available. Should a project become active after this archiving process has occurred, the PM/PX for the project will need to request that the status be changed back to 'Active' and the archive file location be added to the project within the Project Settings. This will also require provisioning a new standard project file directory structure to the current default drive location for the Office Responsibility listed in the Vantagepoint record. This process will return all functions back to normal. The best way to start this process is for the PM/PX to put in a Helpdesk ticket to start the request process.

https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Dialog_Boxes/Save_Markup_Session_dialog_box.htm

Purpose: Newforma Project Information Link enables you to make a connection between your Revit® models and elements and Newforma building models and elements and other project information. Once the links are created, you can synchronize information back and forth between Newforma Project Center and Revit.

Audience: Internal project team members.

Key Features

●       Newforma Project Information Link connects Revit models and elements to Newforma project information.

●       See and track your list of registered Revit models and elements in the Newforma Building Models and Elements activity center.

●       Sync elements, spaces and record documents from Revit into Newforma Project Center and edit extended properties.

●       Mass update elements, spaces, and record documents data using Newforma’s Edit in Spreadsheet tool, then sync changes back to Revit.

●       Create action items and markups linked to a Revit model.

Tasks covered

●        Register an Autodesk® Revit model

●        Sync Newforma elements

●        Create record documents and PDFs from sheets in Revit

●        Create Newforma spaces

●        Use Edit in Spreadsheet to bulk update elements, sheets, or record document data

●        Add action items from Revit models

●        Create markup Sessions from Revit models

 

Register an Autodesk® Revit Model

Before you can connect your Revit model to project information inside Project Center and sync data back and forth, you must register your models within Project Center. You can register multiple models with a single Newforma project. The two options for registering your models explained below.

When registering an Autodesk Revit model, it is best to utilize a central model since it functions as the central organizing model for all team members.

Option 1: Register a model from Project Center:

1.  To register a model from within Project Center, go to the Building Models and Elements activity center and click Register a Model from the Tasks panel.

2.  Fill in the Name and browse to locate the Model File in the Register Building Model dialog box. Fill in any other information as desired and click OK to save.



Option 2: Register a Model from within Revit:

1.     To register a model from within Revit, click Register Model on the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit’s ribbon, and select the project. The model record is automatically created, linked to the model, and appears in the Building Models and Elements activity center.​​​​​​​

Sync Newforma Elements

Newforma elements are used to organize and track information related to objects in your models and can be seen in the Building Models and Elements activity center. Elements can be any building component such as windows, walls, piping, or room tags. Once the elements are created in Newforma you can use various tools to mass update information, and then sync those changes back to Revit.

1.     To synchronize elements from Revit to the Building Models and Elements activity center in Project Center, go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in, located on the Newforma portion of Revit's ribbon, and click on Building Elements > Synchronize Elements.

2.    In the Synchronize Building Elements dialog box, click Add Revit Elements to select the elements you want to synchronize.

3.    Select individual elements in the model or drag to select multiple elements. Once you’ve selected the elements you want, click Finish.

4.     The selected elements appear in the Synchronize Building Elements dialog box. Use the column filters to isolate the elements you want, then mark the checkboxes of the items you want to synchronize. To create additional matching extended properties between Revit and Newforma Project Center, click Sync Settings.

5.    Highlight the Revit property and click Create Matching Extended Property. The property is created.

6.    Select the group for the extended property and click OK. You will now see the new element in the Items to Synchronize list.

7.     Use the edit buttons to edit any Newforma properties. Click OK when complete. The Elements appear in the Building Models and Elements activity center.


Create Record Documents and PDFs from Sheets in Revit

You can easily create record documents and attach PDFs in the Document Control activity center from the sheets in Revit. Once the record documents are created and the files are attached, you can track revisions and issuance of your important construction documents.


To publish sheets to PDF(s)

1.     To create PDFs from Revit, go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit's ribbon and click Document Control > Publish Sheets.

2.     Click Add Revit Parameters if there is a need to include custom Revit parameters for custom sorting of a multi-page PDF.

3.     Click Publish Settings to control PDF print location, print driver settings and PDF naming conventions.

4.     Control the naming of Combined PDFs (similar to individual PDF files). The name may also contain hard coded information.

5.     Click Publish to publish the sheets to PDF.

To synchronize sheets and publish PDFs

The Synchronize and Add Revisions process described here is the recommended method for synchronizing revision data, as it is specifically intended to be used for synchronizing revision data between Revit and Project Center.

1.     To sync and create PDF sheets from Revit to create Newforma record documents, go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit’s ribbon and click Document Control > Synchronize Sheets and Add Revisions.​​​​​​​

2.     After changing any needed settings, click Synchronize and Add Revisions in the Synchronize and Add Revisions dialog box to synchronize sheets and create PDFs.

3.     The record documents appear in the Document Control activity center along with the linked PDFs.

To synchronize sheets

It is recommended that you do NOT synchronize revision data using Synchronize Sheets, as this could cause data inconsistencies between Revit and Newforma. To synchronize revision data, use Synchronize and Add Revisions, as it is specifically intended to be used for synchronizing revision data between Revit and Project Center.

This option synchronizes only the sheet data from Revit to Document Control. This function does not publish PDFs. 

1.     To sync sheets from Revit to create Newforma record documents, go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit's ribbon and click Document Control > Synchronize Sheets.

2.     In the Synchronize Sheets dialog box, click Sync Settings to create extended properties to be synchronized. The Edit Settings for Document Control Properties dialog box opens:

3.     Highlight a Revit property and click Create Matching Extended Property to create a corresponding Newforma property. 

4.     Highlight the Newforma property to change options such as Mapping Behavior and Group Name. Click OK.

5.     In the Synchronize Sheets dialog box, review the information and select the items you want to sync, then click Synchronize to create the record documents.

Create Newforma Spaces

You can take Revit rooms and areas and sync them to Newforma to create spaces in the Spatial Index activity center. Spaces are needed in Newforma if you plan to use the Punch List app. In addition, you can easily mass update items like finishes and other properties once they are in Newforma, then sync that data back to Revit.

1.     To sync spaces from Revit, go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit’s ribbon and click Spatial Index > Synchronize Spaces.

2.     In the Synchronize Rooms, Spaces, and Areas dialog box, click Sync Settings if you want to add, edit or remove any extended properties as described above. Click OK when done.

3.      Use the column filters to isolate the spaces you want, then mark the checkboxes of the items you want to synchronize. Click Synchronize.

4.     The spaces appear in the Spatial Index activity center.

Use Edit in Spreadsheet to Bulk Update Elements, Sheets, or Record Document Data

You can use the Edit in Spreadsheet task in Newforma when editing elements, sheets, or record documents to utilize Excel’s streamlined copy/paste functionality to expedite editing. You can also utilize formulas within Excel to quickly generate various calculated totals. This tool is especially helpful if you want to utilize office staff to edit element, sheet, or record document data who may not be well versed in Revit.

The Edit in Spreadsheet task can also be run from the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit's ribbon.

If you are using Synchronize and Add Revisions to synchronize record document data between Revit and Newforma, you should NOT also edit record document data in a spreadsheet. Mixing synchronization methods can cause data misalignment for your record documents.

1.     To mass update space data, go to the Spatial Index activity center and click Edit in Spreadsheet from the Tasks panel.

2.     When prompted, navigate to a location in which to save the exported data. After saving the file, it opens in Excel. Edit the data as desired, then save and close the file. A message appears prompting you to click OK to re-import the modifications. If you are not ready to import changes, click Cancel to re-import later.

Add Action Items from Revit Model

If you are working in a Revit model and want to add a to-do item for yourself or someone else, it’s easy to add an action item. Once added, it can be accessed from Newforma in the Action Items activity center.

1.     To add an action item, go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit’s ribbon and click on Action Items, then one of the following:

  • Click Identify if you want to add an action item related to the model in general; or
  • Click Identify for Element if you want to add an action item related to a specific element.

2.     Fill out the action item details as desired in the Identify Action Item dialog box. Modify the Subject if needed. If you know who to assign the item to, fill out the Assigned To field, or it can be assigned later. Add any details in the Description as needed. Note the model is indicated on the Related Items tab. Click Create when done.

3.     If the action item is assigned, and the Send change notification email box is checked, an email is created. Review the email and click Send and File in Action Item to send it.


Create Newforma Markup Sessions from Revit Model

You can use the Newforma Markup tools while working in a Revit model. Once added, markups can be accessed from the Markup Sessions activity center.

1.     To mark up a drawing, zoom into the area of the drawing you want to markup. Go to the Newforma Project Information Link add-in located on the Newforma portion of Revit’s ribbon and click Markup Sessions, then one of the following:

  • Click Markup Snapshot if you want to do a markup related to the model in general; or
  • Click Markup Snapshot of Element if you want to do a markup related to a specific element.

2.     Click and drag the Newforma Snapshot camera to select the rectangular area you want to capture for the markup. It appears in the Newforma Viewer. Use the markup tools to mark up

3.     To save a markup session in Newforma, click Save. Modify the Name and/or add Remarks if desired in the Save Markup Session As dialog box. Note that the model appears on the Related Items tab. Click OK when done.

FindTime offers intelligent suggestions on what days and times work best for people within your organization. Propose your selected times to all attendees and allow everyone to vote. ✓ Policy: Password Policy (ServiceNow Link)

Description: Gresham, Smith and Partners Password Policy 1.0 Overview Passwords are an important aspect of computer security. They are the front line of protection for user accounts. A poorly chosen password may result in the compromise of Gresham, Smith and Par…

ID: b33c4b9d-6992-481c-959a-c2b09c401e47

URL: https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/SitePages/Policy--Password-Policy.aspx

Gresham, Smith and Partners
Password Policy

1.0 Overview

Passwords are an important aspect of computer security. They are the front line of protection for user accounts. A poorly chosen password may result in the compromise of Gresham, Smith and Partners's entire corporate network. As such, all Gresham, Smith and Partners employees (including contractors and vendors with access to Gresham, Smith and Partners systems) are responsible for taking the appropriate steps, as outlined below, to select and secure their passwords.

2.0 Purpose

The purpose of this policy is to establish a standard for creation of strong passwords, the protection of those passwords, and the frequency of change.

3.0 Scope

The scope of this policy includes all personnel who have or are responsible for an account (or any form of access that supports or requires a password) on any system that resides at any Gresham, Smith and Partners facility, has access to the Gresham, Smith and Partners network, or stores any non-public Gresham, Smith and Partners information.

4.0 Policy


4.1 General
  • All production system-level passwords must be part of the GS&P's administered global password management database.
  • User accounts that have system-level privileges granted through group memberships or programs such as "sudo" must have a unique password from all other accounts held by that user.
  • Passwords must not be inserted into email messages or other forms of electronic communication.
  • Where SNMP is used, the community strings must be defined as something other than the standard defaults of "public," "private" and "system" and must be different from the passwords used to log in interactively. A keyed hash must be used where available (e.g., SNMPv2).
  • All user-level and system-level passwords must conform to the guidelines described below. 
4.2 Guidelines

A. Password Protection Standards
Do not use the same password for Gresham, Smith and Partners accounts as for other non-Gresham, Smith and Partners access (e.g., personal ISP account, option trading, benefits, etc.). Where possible, don't use the same password for various Gresham, Smith and Partners access needs. For example, select one password for the Engineering systems and a separate password for IT systems. Also, select a separate password to be used for an NT account and a UNIX account.

Do not share Gresham, Smith and Partners passwords with anyone, including administrative assistants or secretaries. All passwords are to be treated as sensitive, Confidential Gresham, Smith and Partners information.

Here is a list of "dont's":
  • Don't write passwords down and store them anywhere, including Palm Pilots, without encryption
  • Don't reveal a password over the phone to ANYONE
  • Don't reveal a password in an email message
  • Don't reveal a password to the boss
  • Don't talk about a password in front of others
  • Don't hint at the format of a password (e.g., "my family name")
  • Don't reveal a password on questionnaires or security forms
  • Don't share a password with family members
  • Don't reveal a password to co-workers while on vacation
  • Don't use the "Remember Password" feature of applications (e.g., Eudora, Outlook, Netscape Messenger)

Here is a list of "do's":

  • If someone demands a password, DO refer them to this document or have them call someone in the Information Security Department.
  • If an account or password is suspected to have been compromised, DO report the incident to GS&P HelpDesk and change all passwords. Password cracking or guessing may be performed on a periodic or random basis by I.T. staff or its delegates. If a password is guessed or cracked during one of these scans, the user will be required to change it.  
B. General Password Construction Guidelines
Passwords are used for various purposes at Gresham, Smith and Partners. Some of the more common uses include: user level accounts, web accounts, email accounts, screen saver protection, voicemail password, and local router logins. Since very few systems have support for one-time tokens (i.e., dynamic passwords which are only used once), everyone should be aware of how to select strong passwords.

Poor, weak passwords have the following characteristics:  
  • The password contains less than eight characters
  • The password is a word found in a dictionary (English or foreign)
  • The password is a common usage word such as:
    • Names of family, pets, friends, co-workers, fantasy characters, etc.
    • Computer terms and names, commands, sites, companies, hardware, software.
    • The words "Gresham, Smith and Partners", "sanjose", "sanfran" or any derivation.
    • Birthdays and other personal information such as addresses and phone numbers.
    • Word or number patterns like aaabbb, qwerty, zyxwvuts, 123321, etc.
    • Any of the above spelled backwards.
    • Any of the above preceded or followed by a digit (e.g., secret1, 1secret)  
Strong passwords have the following characteristics:
  • Are at least fifteen alphanumeric characters long.
  • Are not a word in any language, slang, dialect, jargon, etc.
  • Are not based on personal information, names of family, etc.
  • Passwords should never be written down or stored on-line. Try to create passwords that can be easily remembered. One way to do this is create a password based on a song title, affirmation, or other phrase. For example, the phrase might be: "This May Be One Way To Remember" and the password could be: "TmB1w2R!" or "Tmb1W>r~" or some other variation. NOTE: Do not use either of these examples as passwords!  
B1.  Windows Domain Passwords Policy:
  1. Passwords must be at least fifteen (15) characters long.
  2. The password can not match any of the last 5 passwords used
  3. Passwords do not expire but are required to be changed if there is evidence that the password has been compromised.
  4. Passwords are checked against a Microsoft service that prevents the use of common or known compromised passwords.
C. Application Development Standards

Application developers must ensure their programs contain the following security precautions. Applications:
  • should support authentication of individual users, not groups.
  • should not store passwords in clear text or in any easily reversible form.
  • should provide for some sort of role management, such that one user can take over the functions of another without having to know the other's password.
  • should support TACACS+ , RADIUS and/or X.509 with LDAP security retrieval, wherever possible.              
D. Use of Passwords and Passphrases for Remote Access Users

Access to the Gresham, Smith and Partners Networks via remote access is to be controlled using either a one-time password authentication or a public/private key system with a strong passphrase.

E. Passphrases

Passphrases are generally used for public/private key authentication. A public/private key system defines a mathematical relationship between the public key that is known by all, and the private key, that is known only to the user. Without the passphrase to "unlock" the private key, the user cannot gain access.

Passphrases are not the same as passwords. A passphrase is a longer version of a password and is, therefore, more secure. A passphrase is typically composed of multiple words. Because of this, a passphrase is more secure against "dictionary attacks."

A good passphrase is relatively long and contains a combination of upper and lowercase letters and numeric and punctuation characters. An example of a good passphrase:

"The*?#>*@TrafficOnThe101Was*&#!#ThisMorning"

All of the rules above that apply to passwords apply to passphrases.

5.0 Enforcement


Any employee found to have violated this policy may be subject to disciplinary action, up to and including termination of employment.

6.0 Definitions


?TermsDefinitions?
?Application Administration AccountAny account that is for the administration of an application (e.g., Oracle database administrator, ISSU administrator).?

https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Activity_Centers/Project_Email_window.htm https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Outlook_Add-in/Topics/Welcome_to_the_Newforma_Project_Center_HTML5_Outlook_Add-In.htm https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Reference_Guides/Project_Email_Quick_Reference_Guide.htm#To_file_email_using_the_Newforma-Items_to_File_folders https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Reference_Guides/Project_Email_Quick_Reference_Guide.htm#To_file_email_using_the_File_in_Project_button https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Reference_Guides/Project_Email_Quick_Reference_Guide.htm#To_file_sent_items_using_the_Send_and_File_in_Project_button_in_a_new_e-mail https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Reference_Guides/Project_Email_Quick_Reference_Guide.htm#To_work_with_the_Project_Email_activity_center https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Graphics_Topics/My_Projects.htm https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Outlook_Add-in/Topics/Project_CenterToolbar.htm https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Dialog_Boxes/File_in_Project_dialog_box.htm https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Tip_and_Tricks/Column_sorting.htm#Filtering https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Tip_and_Tricks/Column_sorting.htm#Sorting https://help.newforma.com/Newforma_Project_Center_Twelfth_Edition/desktop/Panels/Tasks.htm

Purpose

Use the Project Email activity center to gain control of the flow of project information into and out of your email Inbox and ensure that project-related email messages are captured as part of the project record. It allows the valuable knowledge that is so often buried in each project team member’s Inbox to be readily available, searchable and usable to the rest of the internal project team.

Audience

Internal project team members.

Key Features

  • File project related email with your project data so your entire team can retrieve, search, and reply to it.
  • Browse, sort, filter, and search the email and associated file attachments that have been filed to the project.
  • Frees up space in your Inbox and frees resources on your mail server.

Tasks covered

The first three tasks explain the three primary ways to file email from Outlook to a project using the legacy Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook. For information on using the current Outlook Add-in, please see Welcome to the Newforma Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook.

  • Move email to the Newforma-Items to File folders
  • Use the File in Project button on the legacy Project Center Add-In from Microsoft Outlook toolbar
  • File sent items using the Send and File in Project button in a new e-mail
  • Work with the Project Email activity center

To file email using the Newforma-Items to File folders

The Newforma-Items to File folders are created in your Inbox for each project added to your My Projects tab in Project Center. Email is moved from the Newforma-Items to File folders into your project folders on your file server so that everyone who has access to the project can view and act upon the information in the email.

1.     To file an email, drag and drop it into the correct project folder within the Newforma-Items to File folder.


2.     These emails can now be seen by all those who have access to the project through the Project Email activity center.

To file email using File in Project

The File in Project option in the legacy Project Center Add-in for Microsoft Outlook toolbar files email to your project immediately. It also allows you to file e-mail to any project. This option can be configured to leave a copy of each email in Outlook after it has been filed.

1.     Select the messages you want to file and click File in Project.


2.     Select the correct project in the File in Project dialog box and click OK.


To file sent items using Send and File in Project in a new e-mail

The Send and File in Project button in a new email or reply allows you to file email to the project as you send an email.

1.     Create a new email as usual.  When you are ready to send the email, click Send and File in Project.


2.     In the File in Project dialog box, select the project you wish to file the email to and click OK.


If you forget to use the Send and File in Project button when sending a new e-mail simply open your Sent Items folder and either drag and drop the email to the appropriate Newforma-Items to File folder or click File in Project.

 

To work with the Project Email activity center

1.     In the Project Email activity center you can display, filter, sort and preview all of the email filed in your project.


2.     Click Open with Microsoft Outlook in the Tasks panel to open the email to forward or reply.

Phishing Emails

Outlook has a built-in tool to report Phishing and Spam/Junk emails. If you are sure an email falls into one of these categories, follow the steps below to report it to Microsoft. This helps to improve email filters and prevent future incidents. If you're ever unsure if an email is suspicious, please reach out to the Help Desk. 


  1. Either open the email or select it to view in the Reading Pane. (Be careful not to open any attachments or click any links). 
  2. In the top-right corner of the email window press the 'Report Message' button
  3. Select either Junk or Phishing depending on the specific email.

Hacked Email Contacts

You may receive a communication from a trusted contact who may themselves have been hacked. If you suspect this has happened, do not reply back to the email. Call the contact directly on a known good phone number to confirm the legitimacy of the email. If you confirm the contact's email account has been compromised, please report the situation to the Help Desk. How To Submit a Help Desk Ticket


Embedded QR code

You may receive an email asking you to scan a QR code with your cell phone to perform an action. Do not scan any unsolicited QR codes. Below are a couple of examples.





SMS Phishing

Phishing attacks can occur over text message as well as email. Attacks like these are often requesting gift cards or information. Below is an example of someone impersonating our CEO. 



If you receive a phishing text message, do not engage with the attacker. Your phone should have the ability to report and delete messages such as this. 


Spam Phone Calls

Both Spam and Phishing attacks can come through phone calls as well. Unfortunately, we are unable to block specific phone numbers. Spammers often spoof legitimate phone numbers, and blocking these could potentially block a client or trusted contact. However, be vigilant if you receive a call you were not expecting or seems unusual in any way.

Dimensions: 1512x1014

There are some subtle differences to the actions required in the RFI and Submittal workflows when using the Review Order function. The Review Order function enables us to dictate the order in which RFIs or Submittals are reviewed and processed.

For the most part the review and recording of a response is the same as any other RFI or Submittal. First you go in to record a response, after you have received notification that you have one for review. With the Review Order function, your email will include the list of reviewers in the order they will receive notification.


Next is to go into Newforma Project Center (NPC) to Record a Reviewer Response.

With Review Order, when you go to Record a Reviewer Response, you will receive an additional dialog box to select who is recording the response.

Here you will simply select yourself from the list and click OK button. This will launch the regular Record a Reviewer Response window.

In this window, it is important to note the two areas that are highlighted. The Action field must be changed to one of the options contained within it. These are Additional Information Needed, Answered, and Not Answered. Use the appropriate one for your response. The Received Via field will sometimes change to different value, and will need to be checked each time. Info Exchange is the proper value for this field.

After you have recorded your response and attached any documentation or markups of received documentation, you will want to look at the bottom of the dialog window.

As you see in this example, you will have an additional selection available to you in the Next Action field. You will need to make sure the Next Action box is checked, and you will want to select forward to next reviewer. After you have verified this information, you will click the Record Response button. This will trigger the Forward for Review dialog window.

All you will need to do here is verify the next person in line (from your original notification email, and then click the Forward button at the bottom of the screen. This will send the information to next reviewer in line and continue the Review Order workflow. Please CC the appropriate Document Control person on these responses so that they will know this has been completed. If you are the final reviewer in the chain, you will select the Email Forwarder option instead of Forward to Next Reviewer when you record your response. This will close the loop and sent to the appropriate Document Control person for final response and closing.

https://vp.greshamsmith.com/gspapps/WhoIsOn/

Here's a quick walkthrough of the WhoIsOn app.  This app allows you to view whether someone is logged onto a shared station and the software that is available. The app is located at the link here: WhoIsOn - Home

Selecting a Shared Station

Select a Shared Station name from the dropdown list and click "Query". This will display information about who is logged onto the computer. Click the "See Software" button to see which programs are installed on that computer.



 


Searching for a Computer Name

 If you'd like to see which programs are installed on a specific computer (example: LT7Y2BN32?), type the computer name into the search box and click "Query." Then click the "See Software" button to see a list of installed programs. 



 




Searching for a Program or Publisher

Enter a program name in the search box and click "Query" to see a list of computers with that program installed. If anyone is logged onto that computer, their name will display in the "Users" column. *** Please note, computers with Lumion installed DO NOT show up in this query by default.  To include Lumion computers in the search results, check the "Include Lumion" checkbox. ***



 





 



See Status for All Shared Stations

Click the "Query All Stations" button to see a list of all shared stations. You'll see who is logged in and you can click "See Software" to see the programs that are installed.  *** The "Query All Stations" process can take several minutes, and you'll see a warning about this potential delay. ***  



 



"See Software" Results

Whenever you click "see software" you'll see programs grouped by Publisher, in expandable groups. You can close the software list by clicking the close button or clicking off the window. Note that "See Software" doesn't search for ALL software by ALL publishers (we don't care about NVIDIA drivers, for example) so as to speed up the search and only show more relevant information.

https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/Lists/Help%20Library/dispform.aspx?ID=137 https://visionapp.gspnet.com/touch/vision/time https://visionapp.gspnet.com/touch/vision/time
?The Deltek Touch Time & Expense app enables employees to enter their time and track expenses for project-based activities directly from their mobile device - saving time, improving accuracy and increasing efficiency. Expenses can be captured in the moment, and receipts can be uploaded directly to Vision. No more handwritten reminder notes, no more lost receipts!

Currently, Expense Reports can be created and submitted via mobile devices - approvals must be done in Vision by the PM, PIC or DVP.



Available for iOS, Android and Windows Mobile devices, the Time & Expense app installs directly from the Apple App Store, Google Play Store or Windows App Store by searching for "Deltek Vision Time & Expense" in the respective App Store. 
 
 

 

Note for Nashville Wi-Fi users

If your mobile device is currently configured to use the "GSPGuest" wireless session. You will not be able to access the Vision Touch Time server. You will need to disable wireless or connect to the correct Nashville wireless session "Wave". The following link contains more information on the Nashville wireless access points (http://gspportal/sites/Information-Technology/lists/Online%20Docs/dispform.aspx?ID=137).

If using a tablet device such as an iPad, viewing the application in a web browser may be the preferred method rather than the mobile app since it will better format to a larger screen. Just bookmark the server URL (https://visionapp.gspnet.com/touch/vision/time) in the the browser of your choice such as Safari.

Setting up Deltek Touch T&E app for the first time:  

After downloading the app, first enter the Server URL:

https://visionapp.gspnet.com/touch/vision/time


 
The first login screen that is presented requires your GS&P Network credentials:
UserID, Password, and Domain ( NASH ).

 
 

After clicking "Log In" it will appear that the same screen has been duplicated, but instead touch the Windows Authentication.On/Off Toggle button to turn on  This will populate the UserID and Password fields for you. Make sure Database GSP is selected and click Log In again at the top right.

 

 Next, it will ask you to create a PIN code for faster logging in upon your next visit.
 
Entering your Expenses:
 Tap the Menu button
located on the top left.
 

If you have any previously created expense reports, they will appear in the Expense Report Selection list, along with their submission status. To resume an unsubmitted expense report, simply highlight the expense report.

  • To create a new expense report, click the + sign.
 

  • Report Name - Name your report something to help you associate these expenses to a trip - .the best practice is to name the expense report using a unique reference to associate expenses as well as to indicate the business purpose.  For instance, CMBM Site Visit (Date).  This will meet the business purpose requirement and allow the user to easily locate the report for future reference.

  • The Report Date field will default to the date you began this expense report.
  • The Amount Advanced field is not used.
 
  • . For the Date, select the date of the expense.
 
  • To begin entering your expenses, click + for additional lines as needed.
 


  • Description - The best practice is to use a unique reference to associate expenses as well as to indicate the business purpose for the description.  For instance, CMBM Site Visit (Date).  This will meet the business purpose requirement and allow the user to easily locate the report for future reference.
  • In the Amount column, type in the dollar amount for the expense.
  • Next, click in the Category field. Select the category from the drop-down that best describes the expense. There is a category for most common expenses, as well as an Other category for expenses not listed.

 

For our example, we have chosen the Meals category.  

 
  • Type in the Business Reason per Project for the expenses to be reimbursed.  If listing a meal you will need to add the names for each attendee in addition to the business reason.  If you choose Mileage add the Business Reason, Travel From/To and number of miles driven.  Vision will calculate the correct total to the expense report.
  • When you are finished, click Done.

 
  • Next, type the project or overhead number for this expense. If you do not know the number click the magnifying glass in the right corner of the box to search by name.  
  • Bill Field -If you type in or choose a project number the Bill field will automatically fill. The expense will be billed to the client as a reimbursable expense. If it is a direct expense you will need to uncheck the Bill box and the expense will be charged as a direct expense.
  • The Account and Net Amount fields will automatically be populated based on your choices in the Category and Amount fields.

  • You can select electronic receipt copies specific to each expense line.

    To add a receipt, click the Camera image to take a photo or the photo image (highlighted below) to select a photo already on your device.

 

 
  •  If you would like to associate your receipt with multiple lines within your expense report, click the Associate with New Lines option. All categories require a document upload with the exception of the mileage category.
  • You can modify the document's description in the Description field and it will copy to the File Name field.
  • Documents must be uploaded before the expense report is submitted.
  • Keep your personal information secure. A receipt is the best option to submit for reimbursement. Federal regulations require businesses to include no more than the last five digits of the card number on electronically printed receipts provided to the customer. If the receipt or proof of payment you are providing does include any personal account information please take necessary steps to redact before attaching and submitting the expense report.

 
  • After entering all necessary information, click Save followed by Submit. This will prompt you to confirm by entering your electronic signature in the form of your PIN created earlier.
  • Before exiting the record, line items without documentation (attaching of a receipt) will be prompted to include an attachment if necessary.

  •  To submit, click the box with an arrow.
  • To save and complete later, click the floppy disk image
  • To enter additional lines, click the +
     

 

 

After entering your electronic signature (PIN)  and pressing "ok" the expense report will be electronically routed to the PM or PIC of the project for approval.

https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/SitePages/Add-a-Conference-Room-to-a-Teams-Meeting.aspx https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/SitePages/How-to-use-a-Microsoft-Teams-Room-Device.aspx

This guide is for using the Channelside Room for meetings.

How to add the Conference Room to a meeting already scheduled or in progress. Click Here

The Channelside Room has a Teams Room System that is can conduct Teams Meetings, Zoom Meetings, and Cisco Webex Meetings. 

For information on using a Team Room System for Online Meetings. Click Here

​​​​​​​The room also can do In Room Only Meetings allowing content to be placed on the TV's.


Channelside Room has two HDMI connections, one in each table.  There are three TV's, one on the short wall with the Room Camera mounted above.  As well as a TV across from each other along the long walls.   The Conference room is controlled by the Teams Room System Touch Panel that is located on the table farthest from the door.  The Touch Panel should wake up automatically when you walk over to it.

If the TV's are Asleep / Blank you will need to turn them on from the Teams Room System Touch Panel.  Press the "Room Controls" button in bottom right corner. 

Select "Settings" and press "On" for each of the three TV's (Center, Left, and Right).  You will never need to turn the TV's off.

Press "Teams" then "Exit" for a Teams Meeting.


In Room Only Presentations:

Channelside Conference room can do in room only presentations.  It is however recommended to always do Teams Meetings and invite the room.

Select "Presentation"


Connect HDMI cable to your laptop.  Your laptop image will be display across all three TV's.   If another laptop is connected to the second HDMI then the TV's will split the images across the TV's.  HDMI closest to short wall will display image on that tv, while HDMI closest to door will show image across the two TV's along the long walls.  You can "Swap Video" of the two to reverse what is shown.  

Select "Presentation" then select which TV to push HDMI signal to

Using the Lavalier Microphones:

The conference room comes with two Lavalier Microphones that can be used for in room presentations or Teams Meetings.  This is handy if there is main presenter that may be walking around the room.   MIC 1 and MIC 2 is located in the top left drawer of the credenza.  


Turn the microphone on by pressing simultaneously on the side of the microphone and then lift up on the case.

Press the power button

On the top of the microphone a Green Light will appears when it is on.


To turn off the microphone repeat the process of opening the microphone and press and HOLD power button till Green Light turns off.

You can "Mute" and adjust the volume of each microphone from the Teams Room System Touch Panel.

Press the "Room Controls" in bottom right corner.

Press "Mics" on left side.  Here you can Mute / Un-Mute. You can also increase each microphone pick up volume. 

Use Lavalier Microphones while in a Teams Meeting:

While in a Teams meeting select the "Three Dots" on the Team Room System Touch Panel, then select "Room Controls".  From there you can Select "Mics" and Mute / Un-Mute and adjust volume.

This guide is for using the Tampa Hub for In-House Presentations.

Tampa Hub is not equipped to do Online Meetings.

The remotes on Cart 1 and Cart 2 are not needed while in the Tampa Hub

Tampa Hub can be equipped with Two TV carts.  Labeled Cart 1 and Cart 2.   Cart 1 and Cart 2 must be plugged into their correct location.  Cart 1 on right hand side and Cart 2 on Left hand side.   The Touch Panel for operating the hub is located behind the wall next to the trashcans.

Cart 1 requires two network cables and power plugged into wall.  All connections are required for TV's to work correctly. 

Cart 2 only requires one network cable and power.

The Touch Panel may be blank, touch it to wake it up and it will display Gresham Smith logo, press again to see main menu.

The system will wake up and default to showing the Wireless Display connection on both TV's. 


Connecting Laptop to the Cart TV's:

Connect your laptop to Tampa Hub and both TV's will show same image.  Or connect the HDMI cable on Cart 1 to Laptop for faster Connection.


Using Lavalier or Handheld Microphone for In-House Audio:

Select "Mics" on touch panel, and Un-Mute or Mute and control pickup of Microphone.  You can also adjust the overall audio levels of the speakers to the far right under Volume.  Red microphone indicates the microphone is muted.

Located in the Audio / Video Closet, across from Channelside Conference Room, on the middle shelf is the two lavalier microphones.  HUB MIC 1 and HUB MIC 2.

Turn the microphone on by pressing simultaneously on the side of the microphone and then lift up on the case.


Press the power button.

On the top of the microphone a Green Light will appears when it is on.

To use the handheld microphone, make sure that the Lavalier microphone 1 is off.  Both the Lavalier microphone 1 and Handheld microphone 1 cannot be used at same time.

Press the power button and it should turn Data led should light up Green.  Press the power button again to turn the microphone off.

To turn off the Handheld microphone press and HOLD power button till Green Light turns off.

This guide is for using the Soho Room for meetings. 

Soho is equipped with a TV and USB Camera / Speaker / Microphone Device.  You can present your laptop with the HDMI cable or connect via Wireless Display.  The TV remote is located to the right and behind the TV.

Online Meetings: This room works with all online meetings (Teams, Zoom, Cisco Webex, Blue Jeans etc...)

Connect to the TV either HDMI or Wireless Display.  To use the Camera / Speaker / Microphone under the TV you will need to connect the usb cable as well.

Power on the TV with the Power button (top left) and Press Source (top right) to select your connection type and press OK middle button.


​​​​​​​Selecting Camera system in Teams:

Connect USB cable to your laptop.  Your laptop should make several "Dings" that is a good thing.

Open Teams and click the dots next to profile picture in upper right corner and select "Settings"

On the left-hand side select "Devices" and change "Audio devices", "Speaker" and "Microphone" to Jabra PanaCast 50

Scroll down a bit and confirm "Camera" is also set to "Jabra PanaCast 50"

When done simply leave the meeting and disconnect any cables.

https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/Online%20Docs%20Attachments/Remote_Desktop_Personal_Computer.pdf https://visionapp.gspnet.com/gspapps/WhoIsOn/


These instructions allow you to connect to any workstation inside the company from a personal Windows PC.


***To open a PDF copy of these instructions that you can save and email to yourself, click the link below***

Remote_Desktop_Personal_Computer.pdf 


1. Click the Start Menu button in the bottom left corner, and search for Remote Desktop. Then click the Remote Desktop Connection program.





2. Click the arrow beside 'Show Options'.




3. Select the Advanced Tab. Then click the 'Settings' button under 'Connect from anywhere'.





4. Select the button 'Use these RD Gateway server settings:'. Enter the following information then click OK:

Server name: rdg.gspnet.com

Logon method: Allow me to select later

Check Bypass RD Gateway server for local addresses

NOTE: You may need to return this setting to its original position to connect to non-Gresham Smith computers.


 


5. If you wish to use multiple monitors with Remote Desktop, click the Display tab and check the "Use all my monitors for the remote session" checkbox.




6. Return to the General Tab. Enter the name of the remote computer to which you would like to connect. If you need to find a Shared Station, use the Search Utility located here: Shared Station  Where it says "Work Computer Name" below, enter the name of the remote computer.






7. You should be prompted to trust the remote system. Click the Connect button. 








8. You may be prompted to verify the identity of the remote computer. Select 'Yes'.




**If this is a Shared Station, always log off of when you are finished to release the resources for someone else.

https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.microsoft.rdc.androidx&hl=en_US&gl=US https://gspnet4.sharepoint.com/sites/Information-Technology/SitePages/How-to-Install-MS-Teams-for-Android.aspx?web=1


These instructions allow you to connect to any Azure Virtual Desktop from an Android Table or Phone.

1. Install the Microsoft Remote Desktop app from the Play store. https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.microsoft.rdc.androidx&hl=en_US&gl=US

2. Launch the Microsoft Remote Desktop app.


3. Click the Accept button

4. Click 'Workspaces' in the bottom-right, then click the + button in the top-right corner, and click Add Workspace

5. Enter this URL and click Next

 https://rdweb.wvd.microsoft.com/api/arm/feeddiscovery


6. Click Next again


7. Log in with your work email address


8. Tap the computer to which you'd like to connect. Refer to these available resources:

General - Office programs, Outlook, etc. 
CAD - Revit, ACAD, Adobe Creative Cloud Civil3D 
Render - Lumion, Enscape

​​​​​​​9. Select the resources you'd like and click Connect

10. Enter your password and click Continue


​​​​​​​

** A few things to note**

  • Teams will run on the Remote Desktop, but if you need to join a meeting it's best to use the Teams mobile app from your phone. The steps to install Teams on your mobile device can be found here How to Install MS Teams for Android 

  • When finished be sure to log off or you will keep the session open for 18 hours. Disconnected sessions will be logged off after 18 hours of inactivity.

https://apps.apple.com/us/app/microsoft-remote-desktop/id1295203466?mt=12 https://visionapp.gspnet.com/gspapps/WhoIsOn/

These instructions allow you to connect to computers that are located in the office from any Apple computer or tablet. 


1. Install the Microsoft Remote Desktop app from the Mac App Store. https://apps.apple.com/us/app/microsoft-remote-desktop/id1295203466?mt=12




2. Launch the Microsoft Remote Desktop app.

3. Click 'Continue' through the microphone and camera prompts:





4. Choose whether you would like the Remote Desktop app to have access to your camera:





5. Choose whether you would like the Remote Desktop app to have access to your microphone:





6. In the Remote Desktop app, click 'Add PC':





7. Under the Gateway options, click 'add gateway'





8. Type rdg.gspnet.com as the Gateway name, leave "Use PC User Account" selected, and click 'Add'





9. Click the 'Display' tab. If you'd like to use all of your monitors durning the remote session, check the 'use all monitors' box:





10. Return to the 'General' tab and enter the name of the remote computer to which you would like to connect. If you need to find a Shared Station, use the Search Utility located here: Shared Station  Where it says "PC Name" below, enter the name of the remote computer. Then, click 'Add'. 





11. The remote computer you've configured is now available for connection. Double-click the computer name to connect:



12. Enter your username using this format: Nash\username, enter your password, and click 'continue'






13. Click continue on the security pop-up. Your remote computer will open in a new window. 






**If this is a Shared Station, always log off of when you are finished to release the resources for someone else.

https://apps.apple.com/my/app/windows-app-mobile/id714464092

?

These instructions allow you to connect remotely to any workstation inside the company from an Apple iPad or iPhone.

1. Install the Windows App Mobile from the App store. Windows App Mobile on the App Store
 




 


2. Launch the Windows App Mobile app. Then click the plus symbol in the top-right corner.




 3.  Select 'PC'. 
 


 4. Select “No Gateway Configured”


5. Enter the following information:

  • Gateway Name/Hostname or IP Address: rdg.gspnet.com

  • Credentials: Use your short username (nash\username) and your computer login password

  • Friendly Name: Gresham Smith RDG
     

6.  Click PC Name/Hostname or IP Address to enter the computer name you wish to connect to:
 

7. Enter the name of the remote computer to which you would like to connect. 




8. Press Save or Done.  From the home screen select the computer you wish to connect to and enter your credentials when prompted. 

  • nash\username is the correct format.

Note: You may also be asked to verify the identity of the remote system. You can select 'Connect always'. Always log off of the remote system when you are finished to release the resources for someone else.
